Educational News

Ministry of Education to Send Personnel to Inspect Education in Sichuan Province 169

Since the reorganization of the Sichuan Provincial Government and the appointment of Commissioner Yang Quanyu as Director of the Education Department, there has been an intention to reorganize the education system in the province and put it on the right track. The Provincial Government previously telegraphed the Ministry of Education to request the dispatch of personnel to inspect and guide the province, so that education in the province could be improved. The Ministry of Education has repeatedly sent personnel to various provinces and cities in recent years to inspect and supervise higher education in the sparrow cities. The dispatch of personnel to inspect Sichuan Province is also in the planning. The province's telegram requesting the reorganization of education in Sichuan Province coincided with the Ministry's plans. It is reported that the Ministry has internally decided to send commissioner Guo Youshou and academic Gu Zhaoyang to inspect education in the province. The order will be announced by the Ministry soon. It is also reported that the Vice Minister of Education has invited the responsible divisions and sections and the personnel who will be inspecting Sichuan Province to discuss the points to be noted in this inspection regarding how to improve the universities (Sichuan University and Chongqing University), secondary schools (the distribution of funding and their establishment), and primary schools (efforts should be made to increase the number of students), as a memorandum for the inspection personnel after their departure in early May.

High School Students in Guangdong Central Stage Strike to Protest Entrance Exams 170

(Hong Kong, 27th) High school students in central Guangdong decided on the 27th to strike in protest against the entrance exams.

China Cultural Construction Association Prepares to Hold First Annual Meeting; Member Representative Assembly Organizational Law Announced; to Be Held in Shanghai on July 1st This Year 171

Since its establishment last year, the China Cultural Construction Association has spared no effort in promoting its affairs, and local branches have been established one after another. At its second board meeting, the association decided to hold its first annual meeting (i.e., Member Representative Assembly) in Shanghai on July 1st of this year, to review the work of the past year and determine the work plan for the future. The Organizational Law of the Member Representative Assembly was drafted by the association's Organizational Group, revised and approved by the second plenary board meeting, and has been notified to all branches across the country for compliance. The Organizational Law of the Member Representative Assembly of the China Cultural Construction Association is recorded as follows: Article 1: This Organizational Law is formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 10 of Chapter 3 of the association's general charter. Article 2: The association's Member Representative Assembly shall be held once a year and convened by the Board of Directors. Article 3: The functions of the association's Member Representative Assembly are as follows: A. Elect the association's directors; B. Amend the association's general charter; C. Review the association's past work; D. Determine the association's work plan; E. Other. Article 4: The generation of representatives of the association's Member Representative Assembly shall be based on the provincial and municipal branches. Each branch may elect and send three to five representatives, the number of which shall be determined by the branch itself and reported to the association for record. Article 5: All current chairman, vice-chairman, secretary-general, executive directors, directors, and alternate directors of the association shall be the ex officio representatives of the Member Representative Assembly. Article 6: All current presidents and vice-presidents and presidents and vice-presidents of the councils of the association's provincial and municipal branches, if not elected as representatives of their respective branches, may also attend the association's Member Representative Assembly, but shall have no right to vote or elect. Article 7: The election of representatives attending the assembly by the provincial and municipal branches shall be conducted by the general membership meeting or member representative assembly of each branch. In cases of special difficulties, the association's promulgated interim regulations on correspondence elections may be applied. However, the election method adopted and the election results shall be reported to the association for record. Article 8: All branches that have not yet been established and are still in the preparatory stage may mutually elect two representatives from the preparatory committee to attend the association's Member Representative Assembly. Article 9: All elected representatives shall bring the branch's certificate of election when attending the association's Member Representative Assembly and register within the time limit stipulated by the association. Article 10: The Member Representative Assembly shall establish a presidium of five to seven members, whose list shall be drafted by the association's chairman and vice-chairman and submitted to the assembly for approval. Article 11: The Member Representative Assembly of the association shall have a quorum of representatives from more than half of the branches. Article 12: The Member Representative Assembly shall establish a secretariat, with a secretary-general who, under the direction of the presidium, shall oversee all matters to be handled by the assembly. Under the secretary-general, there shall be one chief secretary and several secretaries to handle all documentary matters, and one general affairs director and several staff to handle all logistical matters. Article 13: The Member Representative Assembly may establish a proposal review committee to conduct group reviews. The list of committee members shall be drafted by the presidium and submitted to the assembly for approval. Article 14: The right to interpret and amend this organizational law belongs to the association's standing board of directors. Article 15: This organizational law shall be implemented after being approved by the Board of Directors.

China Cultural Construction Association: Deadline for Reading Competition Extended to May 15th to Avoid Disappointing Eager Learners 172

After the China Cultural Construction Association independently organized the National Reading Competition, registration offices were set up at the association's branches in various provinces and cities. Since the start of registration, participation has been enthusiastic, with dozens or hundreds of people registering every day, reflecting the large number of eager learners in our country who wish to pursue in-depth academic research. Because China is vast and the remote areas have inconvenient transportation, the association has extended the original registration deadline of April 30th by half a month to May 15th to avoid disappointing eager learners. This has been notified to the registration offices of each branch for compliance.

In addition, the association's list of required and reference books for the university and middle school groups can be purchased at a special discount from various bookstores. However, according to letters from participating members, the prices of the various books required for the university group are still considered slightly high, and it is suggested that reference books can be purchased as needed, or that three to five members can form a reading group and read in turn. This method can also be considered for adoption and is provided for reference by the members.

Literacy Education Committee: Literacy Promotion Week to Begin on May 1st; Inauguration Ceremony for District Directors and Service Team Leaders to Be Held at the Same Time; Municipal Education Bureau to Convene Recreational Performers Today to Discuss Promotion Methods 173

In order to expand the promotion of the literacy movement, the Municipal Literacy Education Committee has designated a Literacy Promotion Week for one week starting on May 1st, dividing the work into morning, business, academic, recreational, radio, and film activities for seven days. The opening ceremony for Literacy Promotion Week will be held on May 1st, and the opening ceremony for experimental district schools, the inauguration ceremony for the district directors, the chairmen of the investigation committees, and the leaders of the literacy education service teams will be held at the same time. The Municipal Education Bureau will convene a discussion meeting for recreational performers at 9:00 AM today in the lecture hall of the Municipal People's Education Center on Wensiao Road (文廟路) in the Nanshi District to discuss the promotion of the literacy movement and the improvement of recreational activities. The invitees include various recreational groups such as the Shanghai Opera Research Association, the Suzhou Opera Research Association, the Comedic One-Man Show Research Association, the Jianyu Society Pingtan and Ballad Singing Research Association, the Guangyu Society, the Siming Yue Opera Research Association Preparatory Committee, and the Yongyu Society Shanghai Late Book Research Association, and the Weiyang Pinghua Improvement Association, who are preparing to participate in the literacy movement promotion on May 4th, when recreational performers throughout the city will be mobilized.

Merchant Marine Students Request Priority Hiring 175

The Ministry of Transportation, Songhu Merchant Marine College is the only existing maritime school in the country. Today's maritime leaders mostly come from the two classes of graduates of the school. Because generally untrained sailors are still increasing, and the sailor examination has not been concluded as scheduled, the employment prospects of the school's students are becoming increasingly difficult. Therefore, they gathered in panic a few days ago and made three requests to the school and the Ministry of Communications: (1) Please ensure that the Ministry of Communications concludes the sailor examination as scheduled in June this year, and strictly ban current sailors who have not passed the examination, so as to ensure safety and expand employment opportunities. (2) The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is the only state-run shipping agency, and the school is the only national maritime school. Therefore, graduates of the school should have priority in being hired by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. (3) Before having formal employment after graduation, there should be a corresponding living allowance to ensure that they can concentrate on seeking employment and not be forced to seek other solutions due to livelihood pressures midway, and live up to the government's intention of cultivating maritime commerce. It is reported that the school principal, Wu Daming, believes that the students' request is appropriate and has submitted it to the Ministry of Communications for review and approval.

Second District of South Shanghai Establishes Literacy Education Experimental District and Forms Two Committees for Publicity and Investigation 176

Since the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee appointed Song Chun as the director of the Second District of South Shanghai Literacy Education Experimental District Office, it established the District Office in the Municipal People's Education Center. It convened principals of public and private primary and secondary schools, members of the District Party Headquarters and District Sub-Headquarters, heads of public security bureaus and police stations, personnel in charge of security groups, and personnel from other social institutions to discuss the matter at the office. After deliberation, Lu Shuyang and thirteen others were elected as members of the Publicity Committee, and Tang Jingyun and thirteen others were elected as members of the Investigation Committee, and the appointments were approved by the Literacy Committee and issued by letter. Yesterday, the two committees held their first joint meeting to discuss and decide on various methods of publicity and investigation, sparing no effort.

Municipal Education Bureau Sends Yang Jingyi to Study Education in Japan; Ms. Yang Departed for Japan Yesterday 177

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau sent Ms. Yang Jingyi to Japan to study educational administration and politics. Ms. Yang departed from Shanghai yesterday morning on the Shanghai Maru steamship for Japan. Those who went to the pier to see her off yesterday included Zhong Wei Liu Yazi and his wife, Legislator Wu Kaixian and his wife, and many colleagues in the education field. Ms. Yang has served in the education field in this city for many years and has experience in education. After arriving in Japan, she will first enter Waseda University to specialize in educational and youth administration, and then go to various parts of Japan to study educational administration, for a period of about one year before returning to the country.

Referees' Football Match Ends in a Draw: Westerners Score Two Goals in the First Half, Chinese Team Equalizes in the Second Half 184

The football season is nearing its end. Members of the Chinese and Western referees' associations, hearing of a lack of activity, organized a friendly match yesterday at the Shen Garden. Although the teams featured many veterans, some were either too old or had been out of practice for too long to be considered formidable. On the Western side, only seven players arrived, preventing them from forming a full team. Therefore, Yue Xiurong and Chen Shao of the Chinese association temporarily joined as guest players, making the teams relatively equal in strength. The match was divided into two halves, each lasting thirty minutes. Due to the players' waning stamina, everyone played with flushed faces and a mix of serious effort and comical blunders. The Chinese team narrowly escaped defeat, resulting in a 2-2 draw. Referee Zhong Yongsen officiated before an audience of five to six hundred people, making for a lively event.

Under the call to action, the Western team launched a fierce attack. "Chaplin" Yue Xiurong showed no mercy, aggressively attacking the Chinese territory, repeatedly. Haddon, a renowned Western substitute player, seized the opportunity and played with great bravery. Fortunately, Zhou Jia, despite his age, remained alert and managed to deflect several attacks. After a period of chaos, Zhu [unclear] led the charge forward, while Qu Hongren, with a serious demeanor, dribbled deep into the field. However, his feet failed him, and Chen Shao easily intercepted the ball. As the back-and-forth continued, time flew by, and the first half was nearly over.

Afterward, Helly, the mainstay of the Western team, repeatedly attempted to break through and capture the stronghold, but to no avail. In the midst of this stalemate, Helly seized another opportunity, and Zhou Jia, in a panic, not only failed to make a save but also stumbled backward. Helly then gently tapped the ball in, scoring the first goal for the Western team with a score of 1-0. Five minutes later, Helly launched another attack, Zhang Le's attempt to block him failed, and Zhou Jia, resembling a startled bird, watched as Keith Lay slightly moved his foot, resulting in the Chinese team falling behind by two goals.

After the first half, the Chinese team, recognizing their weak forward line, saw Zhu Qiu volunteer his old prowess and rally the team, taking over as the lead striker. Dong Xiaopei then reported for active duty, forming a partnership that proved quite effective. In the Western team's territory, danger loomed. Before long, Ni Xiaoben passed the ball from the right corner, and Qu Hongren touched it with his heel right in front of the goal, resulting in immediate success. From then on, the Chinese team's morale soared.

Qu Hongren, Zhu Qiu, and Shao Yueping launched three fierce attacks in succession, creating immense pressure. Although Chen Shao managed to save each shot, the Western team was significantly shaken. Shortly after, Dong Xiaopei persevered, advancing alone, step by step, along the right flank of the defense. Unexpectedly, he launched a diagonal kick, and Chen Shao was unable to save it, resulting in a 2-2 draw. With their spirits high, the Chinese team continued their relentless attacks, but Qu Hongren's weak footing led to several missed opportunities. As time ran out, each team had scored two goals, ending in a harmonious tie, and everyone dispersed with cheers.

Love Triangle Murder Case Verdict: Liu Jinggui Sentenced to Imprisonment - Totaling Twelve Years, Lu Ming Acquitted 185

(Beiping, 27th) The love triangle murder case at Zhicheng Girls' School was announced by the District Court today. Lu Ming, Liu Jinggui, and others were brought from the detention center to the Grand Court. Chief Judge Yan announced the verdict: (1) Liu Jinggui premeditated murder, but due to mitigating circumstances, the original sentence is reduced by one-half according to Article 77 of the Criminal Law, and he is sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment. The claim of self-surrender is not established. The previous detention period will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. (2) Lu Ming is declared innocent and will be released within days.

After the verdict, Lu requested bail. The presiding judge stated that it is currently unknown whether the prosecutor will appeal, and bail can only be granted after the written verdict is delivered and the appeal period has expired. It is reported that the prosecutor will appeal the acquittal of Lu Ming.

Shanghai Track and Field Team: White Rainbow Team to Hold Sports Meet Today at 2 PM in Hongkou Park 186

The White Rainbow Team, which won the overall championship with a total score of 68 points at yesterday's International Seven-Group Sports Meet, has been recognized by Chinese and foreign individuals as the only strong track and field team in Shanghai. The team members were originally scattered in various locations. This time, due to participating in yesterday's international sports meet, they gathered in large numbers. Therefore, it has been decided to hold a sports meet for all team members at 2 PM today at Hongkou Park, as a comprehensive review of the performance of all team members. Except for the javelin and discus events, which the Public Works Department advised against due to public safety concerns, all other events are fully prepared. However, the star athlete Liu Changchun cannot participate due to a recurrence of a leg injury. Li Shiming is also unable to participate as he has not fully recovered from a previous javelin injury. All other team members will participate. The Suzhou branch team members are also all in Shanghai. It is expected to be a grand occasion. Admission is free; anyone with a park pass can attend. The purpose of this sports meet is that previous competitions have always been dominated by the team's top athletes. Taking advantage of this rare opportunity, the team's unsung heroes can also show their talent.

Chinese-Western Seven-Group Track and Field Meet: White Rainbow Overwhelms Strong Opponents to Win Championship, Sakur Second, Western Youth Third, Breaks Shanghai Records in Nine Events 188

The Chinese-Western Seven-Group Spring Track and Field Meet, with participants including White Rainbow, Sakur, Macklin, Western Youth, Hai Qing, English Inn, and American Public, was held yesterday afternoon at the American Public Sports Field on Beidang Road. The event attracted a large crowd of several hundred spectators. The White Rainbow team, with its gathering of talented athletes and strong overall strength, ultimately won the championship with a significant score of 73 points. Sakur came in second, Western Youth third, Macklins fourth, English Inn fifth, American Public sixth, and Hai Qing last. Yesterday, a total of nine Shanghai records were broken. The scores and results of each team are listed below:

Team Scores

White Rainbow 73 points Sakur 35 points

Western Youth 18 points Macklins 17 points

English Inn 12 points American Public School 6 points

Hai Qing 2 points

Special Achievements

A total of nine Shanghai records were broken. The best of these was Jia Lianren's 2 minutes and 4 seconds for the 880 yards. Li Shiming competed while injured, almost breaking the record. Fu Baolu's 12 feet and 2.5 inches in the pole vault was unmatched. Unfortunately, the height of the wooden frame had reached its limit, leaving the hero with no ground to display his skills. In the medley relay, Liu Changchun ran the fourth leg for 200 yards, gaining a lead of 200 yards over second place. Russian Tom Shevsky's 10 seconds flat in the 100 yards had great stamina, causing Cheng Jinguang to be overtaken. Zeng Rongzhong's performance in the 440 yards, where he surged to the championship in the final 110 yards, was a masterpiece. Yesterday, the White Rainbow team was full of talent and can be considered a great success.

International Hopes

Yesterday's sports meet served as a prediction for the upcoming international track and field meet. Although the achievements of the Chinese athletes were not yet fully satisfying, they were more than enough to overwhelm other countries. Except for Russian Prokofyev, who won three gold medals, the other countries had mediocre and unremarkable talent, demonstrating the decline of international talent in Shanghai. It is a pity that our country's shot putters, Chen Baoqiu and Leng Peigen, have not shown any progress.

My Philosophy as a Basketball Referee (4) 197

— By Mr. Dahl of the United States, Translated by Qian Yiqin

Mechanical Procedures. A few more points regarding mechanical procedures and physical condition remain. When a single referee is officiating, it is best to be constantly in front of the offense, in this position, all of the play can be clearly observed. This means that the referee must quickly move his position to the other end of the court whenever the offensive team changes. This is not impossible, because the referee will soon be able to move in time to the main part of the court, and from that position, any direction can be reached. Sometimes it is difficult to quickly follow the offense and move to one end of the court, or stay behind the ball and the offense, but one should not stay behind the ball and the offense, but immediately move to the front of the offense. This requires a strong physique, which goes without saying.

Physical Condition. The physical health of a successful referee is as important as that of a player in an actual game. Therefore, one must always train. Regarding the physical condition of a referee, it is often mentioned in terms of one's "breath," but in the author's opinion, the condition of one's "legs" is more important than "breath." Therefore, a referee is only as strong as his weakest leg. If his legs cannot quickly bring him to the front of the offense, his efficiency as a referee will be reduced. Although his eyes are as sharp as when he was young, he cannot stand far across the court and call a foul as well as when he is in front of the ball. His legs must lead his eyes to the most easily seen position. Therefore, when his legs are no longer capable, it is better for the referee to decide to put his old whistle on the shelf and retire permanently.

If a referee takes his work seriously, he should train his body to a strong condition before the start of the basketball season. One should never officiate the first game of the season without any preparation. It is best to consult with the coach and practice playing ball before the start of the season. This will not only train the body but also train the eyes. It is not a good practice to start officiating official games and receive school compensation from the beginning. It is better to use it as practice refereeing. Such practice and preparation should be done before the start of the season.

Two-Referee System. This article cannot be considered complete if it does not mention the two-referee system. The two-referee system can be divided into two types, which I think are known to most readers. In one system, both referees proceed along the sidelines of the court, each calling fouls according to what they see, regardless of where they are. In another system, one referee controls one side of the court, and when the offense moves to the right side of the court, he moves to the basket and watches the offense coming towards him. The other referee moves down along his side, following behind the offense. If the direction of the offense changes, the latter gradually moves to the opponent's basket, and the former follows behind the offense. Thus, there is always one person in front of the offense and one person behind. The author believes that this system is better than the other system, where one person only controls one side of the court and there is no designated person responsible for the play under the basket.

If two people only move back and forth along one side of the court, it is easy for both people to focus on the actions near the ball, and there is no designated person responsible for the fixed parts of the court. It is common to encounter the problem of simultaneously whistling to announce the same action, and each person cannot decide who should call the foul, or wait for the other person to call the foul, resulting in both people abandoning this duty and responsibility.

The secret to the success of the two-referee system lies in two principles: first, one person must always be in front of the offense and迎之; second, the other person must always be behind the offense and追之. Regarding the relationship between the two referees, the most important thing is that the referee behind the offense must know and feel when he should not blow his whistle.

The person on the court and under the basket should be fully responsible for the actions in that area, because he is in the best position to observe all the actions. With this responsibility clearly defined, the person behind the offense will not be forced to call everything in front of the court, because he cannot call them because his position is not suitable for observing the game. The most difficult situation to discern is when a player is closely guarding someone who is about to make a basket. The referee in front of the offense only sees a legitimate defense, while the referee behind the offense calls a holding foul, which is actually not a foul. The person behind the ball sees it as if it were a foul, so he calls it, but he should not do this and should let the referee in front take the initiative and call everything. This is a difficult situation and will only be successful when both referees are used to working together. However, the referee behind the ball should of course also call fouls in front of the court, but this must be a very obvious foul or violation, especially when the companion in front is far away from the game and in a difficult position to see. The referee behind the ball should call it only if they practice cooperation and the one behind is always careful to blow the whistle, and the above difficulties can be resolved.

In all respects, this system has many advantages over the system where two people only officiate along the sidelines of the court. Because each person's area is defined and they feel responsible within their area, they do not need to worry about whether the other referee will call a foul, nor do they need to worry about their own whistle blowing, thus avoiding the problem of omissions. This system also eliminates the problem of one person working while the other watches, or one referee calling before the other. Because the responsibilities are divided, many whistles can be avoided, resulting in excellent refereeing.

Conclusion. In conclusion, it should be clear that the referee is responsible for the game regardless of whether the outcome of the game is satisfactory or not. He is temporarily a representative of the rules committee, which is of great significance to the committee, because today there are often people who want to criticize the committee's decisions.

This responsibility is always present, and from the perspective of the game of basketball, it is better to have a satisfactory outcome than an unsatisfactory one. The referee cannot avoid being criticized or praised. The referee is best to find inner satisfaction in his good refereeing. To seek satisfaction, one must follow the rules outlined above.

The public's criticism is as changeable as the weather. The author recalls a time when the two sides were enemies, because the key to winning the championship was that if one team won, the championship would be taken away, and if the other team won, the scores would be equal, and they would have to play again. Therefore, the competition was extremely fierce. As a result, the team that could immediately win the championship lost by two points, causing the two referees who officiated the game to be slightly criticized. A commentator for a certain newspaper believed that the two people failed to handle the game well and caused too many fouls, so harsh comments were added to them. A week later, the two teams fought for the final championship. Because of the suppression of the referees (the two people were hired from another city), the game was very clean. After this excellent game, the newspaper commentator from last week, who had severely criticized the referees for being too strict, now accused the two referees of being too focused on fighting. One should know that dissatisfied people often like to criticize in order to achieve their private desires, and the spread of criticism is extraordinarily rapid. As for conscientious referees and well-officiated games, they never brag. Although, unfair criticism will eventually be like the flowing water of the east, gone forever. (End)

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

How to Be a "Scientific Child" 198

— Jun Peng

Weapon Materials There are no waste products in the world, only wasteful people. Those who don't know how to use waste products are wasteful people. When we poor children play scientific tricks, how can we afford any scientific instruments? Bamboo heads, wood scraps, cotton, rags are all raw materials for making guns and bullets. If you come across cake boxes, glass bottles, tin cans, needles, rope, ink bottles, iron wire, etc., you must save them to prepare for future weapons.

Self-Made Guns We need to build guns for combat, but foreign instruments are very expensive. Then, we have to make our own instruments, that is, use those many wastes mentioned earlier. Don't have an alcohol lamp? Use an ink bottle to imitate a small alcohol lamp. Don't have a soft cork? Wrap it with cotton and cloth. Don't have methylated spirits? Just distill the liquor. Don't have glass? Find a few thin bamboo tubes or wax paper tubes to replace them. Children! I just give a few examples, but it's up to your smart brains to use them. If you really can't do it yourself, then go out and buy them.

Losing Battles A scientific child is not afraid of failure. If the trick is not successful, don't be discouraged, don't be tired. If you fall, get up and try again. You must achieve the goal. Failure is our greatest teacher. We must have an indomitable spirit to create a "scientific child." If you have little contact, you will run away, this is definitely not a scientific child, and you will never be able to take on the mission of creating a "scientific China"!

The Story of Su Qin 199

— Tu Hongxia

During the Warring States period, there was a man named Su Qin from Luoyang. He was a strategist. Initially, he went to persuade King Hui of Qin, but King Hui did not believe him. As a result, he was unsuccessful and returned home. All the clothes and travel expenses he had taken with him were used up, and he was in a sorry state. When he returned home, his wife, sister-in-law, father, and mother all ignored him. When his clothes were torn, his wife refused to mend them. When he was hungry, his sister-in-law refused to give him food.

He felt extremely unhappy, so he resolved to study hard. Late at night, when he was tired and wanted to sleep, he would prick his thigh with an awl, and the blood would flow to his feet. Startled awake, he would continue reading. After studying for three years, he went to the State of Zhao. The King of Zhao trusted him greatly and appointed him as Prime Minister. After becoming an official and returning home, his wife, sister-in-law, father, and mother all rushed to greet him from afar.

Children, you must know that the result of suffering is happiness!

Diamond 200

— Zhen

One Sunday, Le'er and Hua'er went to the bustling market to buy some things. They passed by a hardware store and saw a person using something like a pencil to score glass. In a short while, the glass was neatly cut.

"Brother, look, how can that pencil-like thing cut glass?" Hua'er asked his brother in surprise.

"That thing is made of wood, and at the end, there is a very small diamond. It's just like the diamond ring we see Mom wearing on her finger, only bigger. Because diamond is a very hard crystal, it can cut glass." Le'er replied.

"Aren't diamonds very expensive? I heard that Mom's ring cost several thousand dollars. Then that wooden stick for cutting glass must cost dozens of dollars, right? Is that so?"

"That's not necessary, it only costs a few dollars because it's man-made."

"Huh! That's strange! Can diamonds be man-made? Then how are they made?"

"Man-made diamonds are not much different from natural ones. Man-made diamonds are just smaller crystals. Natural ones are not very beautiful in shape and must be polished to have a beautiful luster. The method of making man-made diamonds is to dissolve pure carbon (by charring white sugar) in molten iron, then throw it into cold water. The iron will suddenly solidify, and then a chemical is added to dissolve the iron, and a man-made diamond can be obtained."

So Hua'er bought his things and quickly went home to try it out.

The Wonderful Number Guessing 202

— Yide

Sister said to her younger brother, "We have nothing to do right now. Let's play a math game, okay?"

The younger brother said, "Great! I like all games! Please tell me the rules of the game."

The sister said, "You prepare a piece of paper and a pencil. Without me seeing, you write down a two-digit number at random."

The younger brother hurriedly wrote the numbers "32," and said, "I've already written them down. What do I do next?"

The sister said, "You multiply the first digit by two, then add one; after adding, multiply by five; after multiplying, add the second digit. After you calculate this, tell me the answer, and I will know the two-digit number you originally wrote."

"Wow! That's amazing!" Saying that, he started calculating:

The younger brother said, "I've calculated it. The answer is thirty-six. Please guess!"

The sister, without thinking, smiled and replied, "The two-digit number you wrote down at the beginning wasn't '31', was it?"

"Haha! That's exactly right! What method did you use to guess it?"

The sister said, "The method is simple and unremarkable. I just need to subtract five from your answer in my head, and I'll get it. Think about it, thirty-six minus five is thirty-one, right?"

The younger brother let his sister guess several more times, and she guessed correctly every time. The younger brother was extremely happy. The younger brother said, "Tomorrow I'll go to school and let my classmates guess!"

Literacy Campaign 203

— Zhang Yian Photo

Kite 204

— Ding He

The spring weather is exceptionally pleasant. The spring breeze is blowing gently, making it perfect for flying kites on the grass. Today, let's study kites together:

(1) Why do kites rise? The rising of a kite relies on the resistance of the air, which generates a lift force to push the kite into the sky (as shown in Figure A). The stronger the wind, the greater the lift force, and the higher the kite rises. If the wind is small, the lift force generated is small, and the kite cannot be flown. However, whether the string (belly string) on the kite is tied properly or not can also affect the magnitude of the lift force. If the string is tied too straight, with a large angle, the lift force generated is too small (as shown in Figure B). The wind creates a vortex on the back of the kite, increasing the pressure on the kite and adding to its weight, making it impossible to fly. However, if the string is tied too slanted, with a small angle, the kite also cannot be flown. We know that if the weight of the kite is greater than the lift force, it will definitely not be able to fly.

(2) How to Make a Kite: Now that we understand the principle of kite flying, making a kite is relatively easy. Materials for making a kite: bamboo, mulberry paper. Tools: knife, scissors, glue. Split the bamboo into thin strips with a knife, making sure they are evenly thick. Then (in Figure 2), choose the shape you like and tie them together. After tying them together (as shown in Figure 3), dab on some red ink or black ink to enhance the kite's appearance.

If the kite we tied leans to one side after being flown (as shown in Figure 4), it means that the leaning side is heavier. We should try to lighten the leaning side or add an equal amount of weight to the other side (the lighter side).

Children, look at how much fun they are having flying kites in Figure 5. Let's also make a kite and try it out!

Children's Bank 206

— Chonglou

There are various banks in society, and now I want to advocate for a "Children's Bank"; but this "Children's Bank" that I advocate is not for saving money, but for saving wisdom.

Because when people are young, their food and clothing can be provided by their parents, and they don't have to bear the responsibility of economics themselves. They can devote their energy to their studies; so the "Children's Bank" that I am now advocating is to increase the strength of children's learning.

Here, let me list two articles of the "Children's Bank" charter below—

"Lump-sum withdrawal of regular savings"; This method requires children to accumulate their knowledge slowly, and then take it out for application when they have accumulated a whole. For example, if you want to be a scientist, then you should deposit the scientific knowledge you have learned in the bank uninterruptedly. After ten years, you will definitely be able to become a great scientist who can invent things.

"Withdrawal of regular savings at any time", This article requires children to store what they have learned at ordinary times and then take it out for application at any time. For example, today you learned arithmetic from the teacher, you store it in the bank, and when you have to calculate accounts for buying things at home tomorrow, you take this arithmetic out for application...

Children! Are you willing to enthusiastically participate in this convenient and stable "Children's Bank" as its depositor?

Children's New Life 207

— Ba Ling

Now is the time when the New Life Movement is being vigorously promoted. Adults must, of course, follow the items of the New Life and do them earnestly. However, children are the future masters of the country and the reformers of society, and they must especially work hard to implement the New Life. In my opinion, children's new life must at least achieve the following things to be called a new child:

(1) Get up early every day, brush your teeth, take deep breaths, and do calisthenics.

(2) Arrive at school on time to study, and show appropriate politeness to teachers and classmates.

(3) Concentrate on listening in class; do not cheat during exams.

(4) Chew food carefully, and take a walk for half an hour after drinking, avoiding strenuous exercise.

(5) Books and objects must be organized clearly, and not be messy or damaged.

(6) Be able to help parents at home and do what you can.

(7) Do not quarrel with siblings, and always show courtesy and respect in your behavior.

(8) Do not develop bad habits, and regard smoking and gambling as harmful demons, and resolve not to approach them.

(9) Always find ways to help others anytime, anywhere.

(10) Clothes should be changed often, and the body should be bathed regularly.

Eradication of Microbes 208

— Ren Chaojun

Microbes are terrible microorganisms. If they enter the lungs, they can cause various diseases. Their traces are everywhere—whether in the air, on utensils, or on clothes.

Indeed, it is not easy for microbes to reach the inside of our bodies. If they enter through the nasal cavity, nasal hairs will block them. If they get past the nasal hairs, then the felt hairs on the inner wall of the trachea will catch them. If they enter through the oral cavity, the saliva in the oral cavity can prevent their reproduction. If they remain in the nostrils, oral cavity, and trachea, the mucous membrane there is not very suitable for their reproduction. As for them entering through broken skin, white blood cells inside will kill them, but this is only for healthy people. They can still reach the inside of weakened bodies, so we should strengthen our bodies and eradicate the bacteria nearby.

Regarding methods of eradication: 1. Mix hot lime and water and use it to brush walls and pour it into drains and toilets. 2. Use formaldehyde gas to kill microbes in rooms. 3. Eliminate their vectors—flies and mosquitoes. 4. Boil clothes in boiling water to kill microbes. Other methods include drinking boiled water, ensuring that rooms have plenty of sunlight, and breathing fresh air.

Children, now is spring, the season when they multiply. We should quickly eradicate them to avoid the occurrence of various infectious diseases in the summer.

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (15) 209

— Xin Qing

I thought that dying slowly in that dark tomb seemed worse than any other fate. I thought that even giving those savages a meal was not half as unfortunate as this.

The day came when I was to be lowered into the tomb on the mountaintop. As usual, I was wearing my best clothes and precious stones. Because I was such a big figure locally, the king and queen, along with a large crowd, came to the tomb entrance to see our end.

My wife's body was lowered first, followed by me in an uncovered box with a pot of water and a few small loaves of bread. Then I was lowered down, and the tomb entrance was sealed.

When I looked around, I saw that I was in a kind of large cave, a hundred yards deep. All the precious gems and beautiful clothes of the dead were everywhere on the ground, and there were white bones of the dead all around.

I sat on the ground crying, thinking that my life would end in this way. I thought that even if I had lost my life in the wind and waves at sea, it would be the same as this strange death.

However, spending time on such thoughts was useless to me, so I ate a piece of bread and drank water from the pot. Thus, I stayed well in the tomb for several days. As you listen on, you will know that trying to save myself was a good thing.

One day I heard a sound, as if some creature was moving. I walked towards the source of the sound, but the thing ran away as I approached. I continued on, and soon I saw a glimmer of light shining like a star.

I kept moving forward, and finally, imagine how happy I was—I found that the light was coming through a large hole in the rock. When I walked out of this hole, I saw that it led to the seashore. The sound I had heard turned out to be an animal that came out of the sea every day, passed through the hole in the rock, and came to the cave to eat the dead.

Once I determined that I was safe in this place, I knelt on the beach to thank God for protecting me. After I rested for a while, I returned to the cave to retrieve the food that was left behind. There, I took the best gems and the food I could find, and then returned to the seashore.

Spring Sun 210

— Rong Yu

Spring sun! You smile with a gentle face: You wear a warm smile, you are truly a loving mother in nature. Little birds sing for you: Hundreds of flowers are dedicated for you to see: Small grasses, tall trees, wearing green clothes, happily dance. Looking at this crowd of children, you must have extraordinary comfort in your heart.

Spring sun! You are like an alarm clock, awakening many sleeping little animals. Look, the bee brother is out working; look, the butterfly sister is out dancing; and there are countless small companions singing and jumping. Even our children take off their light clothes, perk up their spirits, and play on the grass. Looking at this crowd of children, you are probably smiling so much that you can't close your mouth.

Spring sun! You are truly our loving mother, may you always stay in the human world and protect this group of innocent and lively children with no selfishness.

Conflicting Financial News, Chaotic Gold Standard Pricing – Ended with a Rebound of More Than Two Yuan – Once Reached a New Price of 741.5 Yuan in the Morning Session – Suspension of Silver Purchases Triggers Large Buying Volume 212

Rice Prices: Weak in the South, Strong in the North; Soybean Market Almost No Transactions 222

Japonica rice from Shanghai's southern sources arrived in only about twenty-odd shipments yesterday (totaling nearly 4,000 shi), and sales were sluggish, whether wholesale or retail. Very few transactions were opened for each type of rice, making it difficult for the market to show improvement. A trend of stabilization with slight softness was observed. The prices of both thick and thin japonica rice had already been reduced by several fen. Given the abundant stockpiles in the port and the unusually volatile market conditions, a positive outlook for the future is unlikely. The price of silver taels remained relatively stable. From Shanghai's northern sources, there were seventeen or eighteen shipments. On the market, shipments of white japonica rice saw some movement, and transactions for early thin japonica rice were quite active. Other types of rice were normal. The market price of white japonica rice increased slightly by several fen, and the price of early thin japonica rice increased by several fen to one jiao. Silver taels turned stable, and the prices of other types of rice remained firm.

The market for foreign indica rice has revived. Foreign rice is being shipped inland, with recent shipments not only drawing from existing stockpiles but also with merchants directly distributing to customers. Over the past two days, rice shops like Zhongshan Changyi distributed over 30,000 packages to the Hangzhou-Shaoxing area, and various regions in Jiangsu and Zhejiang also directly received shipments. The total volume was also around 40,000 to 50,000 packages. Therefore, market transactions have slightly decreased, with yesterday's total transactions falling short of 10,000 packages. However, the market remains stable due to sustained real demand. There was also some speculative buying and reselling of future foreign rice, with 1,200 tons of cargo in transit, mostly destined inland. Future rice and some foreign rice were handled by local businesses. Recently, the price of gold has fallen, potentially allowing for a slight reduction in the production price of foreign rice. However, local rice prices are rising, making the price difference similar. Yesterday, customer indica rice was actively purchased for inland regions, and with low inventory levels, 2,000 packages were sold at a price increase of two or three fen.

Due to sellers' unwillingness to sell at low prices and buyers' reluctance to pay high prices, the soybean market entered a wait-and-see mode. Some inland and local small millers were active, opening transactions for 200 packages of Dalian Sipingjie soybeans at a price of four yuan and four jiao seven fen, and 500 packages of Hankou zha beans at a price of three yuan eight jiao one fen to eight jiao. 320 packages of Hankou gou beans were traded at a price of four yuan zero eight fen to four yuan.

Silk and Tea: Keemun Black Tea Opening Prices 223

Tea merchants have received the news that Keemun black tea opening prices were set yesterday. The price for superior Dafang Gaozhuang tea was reported at eighty yuan, and the price for Keemun County tea was set at sixty yuan. Most other villages were around seventy yuan, with prices higher than in previous years. However, the weather is clear, and the quality of the tea leaves is excellent. Various tea companies have already started processing, creating a lively atmosphere.

Yesterday, the sugar market saw continued sharp declines in customs gold, reaching as low as 1.610, leading to further weakening and continued price drops. The association set the price for 24 coarse white sugar at sixteen yuan and seven jiao, a decrease of three jiao. Spot re-exports were priced at five yuan and four jiao, a decrease of one jiao, and forward contracts at five yuan and two jiao five fen, but no transactions occurred. Guangdong coarse white sugar was priced at sixteen yuan and seven jiao, with some sales. The factory's refined white sugar fell another two jiao, with Zhenyu No. 1 at sixteen yuan three jiao, No. 2 at two jiao, No. 3 at zero five fen, and No. 4 at fifteen yuan nine jiao. Chaoqing sugar, due to a further decrease of over ten yuan in Shantou exchange rates, reached one thousand and three yuan, leading to an increased cost of several jiao and further divergence from the Shanghai market. Branded goods are holding firm.

Women's Corner

Men and Women Competing for Occupations 225

— Chen Yan

In truly feudal societies, women were entirely slaves to their families. Their livelihoods were determined by "obeying their fathers when young, their husbands when grown, and their sons when widowed." Their life and death were entirely controlled by these men, with no direct connection to society. However, the massive influx of foreign capitalism shattered our dilapidated and backward screens. Rural areas went bankrupt, and the large family system collapsed. Years of internal and external troubles have fulfilled the proverb of "nine out of ten houses empty." Therefore, despite one side advocating for virtuous wives and good mothers, urging "Nora" to return home, the fathers, husbands, or sons upon whom women depended for life and death were being cast aside from the production line in nine out of ten households. In this situation, women had no choice but to enter society in search of survival.

On the other hand, factory owners and merchants sought profit. Thus, they happily employed women who were cheaper and more hard-working and compliant than male workers—women who were previously only fit to be household slaves. Female clerks, in addition to the above conditions, further leveraged their looks as live advertisements to attract customers. This has precedents in various countries. China is also heading down this path. The problem that arises here is the competition for jobs between men and women. According to a report in the Sino-Japanese Daily on the 20th of this month, there is news of occupational conflict between male and female waiters in Guangzhou restaurants and tea houses: The Guangzhou Restaurant and Tea House Workers' Union recently petitioned the government to prohibit the employment of female waitresses in city restaurants and tea houses, arguing that they were seizing jobs and affecting the livelihoods of union members. This attracted the attention of the Women's Association, leading to a dispute. According to Ms. Peng of the Women's Association, "Women's liberation aims to achieve equal education and economic independence. Economic independence depends on occupation. Women can fill any occupation that men can fill. European and American countries have absolutely no restrictions on women's occupations. The women's rights movement in this province is just beginning to sprout, and women's occupations are gradually expanding, such as female civil servants in government agencies, school teachers, hospital doctors and nurses, ushers in entertainment venues... All have women in these roles. Anyone with a clear understanding of global trends should promote women's occupations to foster mutual assistance between husband and wife. The Restaurant and Tea House Workers' Union considers the employment of female waitresses as seizing jobs, which shows a lack of understanding of the trend of the women's rights movement... We are all human beings. We should only ask whether they have the skills to perform the job, and there should be no distinction based on gender. Our late Premier advocated for equality between men and women and the promotion of women's rights, and this is clearly stipulated in the party platform. Our association, as the leading organization for women from all walks of life, believes that this matter hinders the development of women's occupations and will fight for women's rights based on reason in the coming days." The labor union committee, on the other hand, said, "The number of unemployed restaurant and tea house workers has reached over five or six thousand. Female waitresses rely on their looks to cater to the psychology of customers. They have no specialized skills or business experience for restaurant and tea house work and are merely used by profit-seekers to exploit social weaknesses to attract customers. The result is only the trampling of women, creating social unrest. In fact, the issue of promoting women's occupations needs to be carefully considered, including which jobs are suitable for women and which can lead to their downfall. This issue is extremely important. Therefore, our association's opposition to female waitresses is not to suppress the development of women's rights but to protect the job security of our union members and indirectly improve the status of women. It is purely a matter of morality." Therefore, their petition to the five party and government agencies contains even more wonderful phrases, such as "At a time when we are promoting old morals and saving declining customs, we must not allow cunning merchants to pursue only personal gain, creating abnormal development and causing social disputes."

After reading the above excerpts from speeches and petitions, it seems that everyone has their own reasons, and both sides are justified. As for who will ultimately win, it is difficult to predict at this time. However, in recent years, a wave of revivalism has swept through Guangdong. The union is seizing on the authorities' mentality of promoting old morals, and perhaps another ban will be issued, granting them a temporary victory? However, as the economic downturn intensifies, businesses, in addition to closing down, must struggle to survive and will seek profitable avenues, regardless of how strict the bans may be, and will sometimes try to implement them secretly. It has been previously decreed in Guangdong to prohibit the employment of female waitresses in restaurants and tea houses. The fact that female waitresses are now being rehired is clear evidence. On the surface, it seems that the final victory will ultimately belong to the Women's Association. However, it is necessary to say a word to the women's rights movement: this kind of dispute can be seen as an anti-revivalist movement, but the ultimate goal of the women's movement is not merely to compete with men for occupations. Instead, it should be based on the entire social and economic problem, seeking true equality between men and women.

Women's Issues Lecture Series

Section 2: Feudal Housewives and Marriage 226

— Jun Hui

The feudal state, built upon the labor of serfs, was necessarily a deliberative body of lords, nobles, monks, and bureaucrats. To plunder the wealth of neighboring countries, to suppress the rebellions of serfs, and, more importantly, to legally and limitlessly exploit the masses of peasants, the state apparatus was endowed with absolute autocratic power, and the wielders of this power were the lords. However, to exercise their autocratic power, lords needed a certain legal and moral order, which gave rise to feudal codified law and moral codes. This law naturally presupposed absolute subordination. In other words, there were certain legal and moral relationships of subordination among adults, between men and women, between parents and children, and between elders and juniors. The most typical features of this were the feudal status system and the feudal moral codes that oppressed women.

The status system was a system used by feudal states to regulate the status of people of all social classes through law. For example, lords, nobles, monks, merchants, artisans, and serfs all had certain social statuses, as well as certain top-down relations of domination. There were clear distinctions in their family, religious, moral, educational, and all social lives. For example, a merchant could not sit in the chair reserved for nobles, could not receive the education of nobles, and, more importantly, could not marry into the nobility. Under this system, the family life and marriage forms of the various social classes naturally differed greatly. I would like to briefly describe here the lives of women of lords, peasants, and merchants and artisans.

First of all, the lord's family fully reflected the characteristics of his social status. To maintain power over his subjects and people, the lord needed to strengthen his patriarchal authority. He held the power of life and death over his family, transforming his children into property, transforming them into non-personal objects. However, as the lord's constant work was war and plunder, he had to entrust domestic affairs to his most trusted wife. Thus, the lord's wife, in the capacity of the mistress of the house, managed the organization of production, the collection of taxes, the storage of grain, and various other household affairs. This mistress had the right to harshly exploit the serfs and to execute unceremonious punishments. However, she was in an inhuman position, similar to that of a serf, towards her husband, the lord.

Marriage in the lord's family was thoroughly predicated on the interests of the family. In detail, the marriage between lords and nobles was a kind of contract for political and economic purposes. In order to conclude a solid alliance, to increase the family's economic strength, and, more importantly, to guarantee military security, one could marry one's young daughter to an old lord in a neighboring region. Personal love and desire had to be sacrificed under the great premise of family interests. Engels said:

"For the nobility and the knights, as for the ruling monarchs, marriage was a political act, a transaction by which their power was to be increased through new alliances; the interests of the dynasty, not those of the individual, were decisive."

This strategic marriage gave rise to the bad habit of early marriage. Early betrothals were prevalent among noble families in medieval Europe. A countess betrothed her young daughter to the heir of the German duchy of Berthold, and the bride and groom were not even six years old. This bad habit can still be seen in our country today.

Secondly, the women of peasant families participated in all productive labor just like serfs, but the feudal moral concept of male superiority also dominated their lives, and peasant women became serfs of serfs. However, their marriage and family relations were often directly dominated by the lord. The lord regarded the marriage between serfs as a means of increasing his own labor force. On this basis of interest, he would directly handle their marriage. Seshukav said:

"They (the lords) regarded the marriage of peasants in the same way as the mating of horses and dogs to breed offspring and bring benefits to the lord."

In this way, the lord could forcibly marry farmers over the age of eighteen and farm women over the age of fourteen, because they keenly felt that the increase in the number of serfs was the source of their increased benefits. Furthermore, feudal law not only gave the lord the right to arbitrarily dispose of the labor and property of peasants, but even gave him the possibility of extensive sexual coercion. This point will be detailed in the "First Night Right" section.

Finally, the families of merchants and artisans were the predecessors of modern bourgeois families. In the closed natural economy era of the Middle Ages, specialist occupations in handicrafts and commerce arose under the cities where the lords lived to supply the needs of the lords. Although they were under the domination of the lords just like the serfs, their lifestyles had already adopted progressive forms. Their family forms and the status of women will be described in detail in the sixth lecture. Due to space constraints, no further explanation can be given here.

After Watching the Play *Wu Song* 227

— Bi Yao

It has been ten years since I last watched traditional opera. Last Saturday night, at the invitation of a friend, I stepped into a certain theater. At that time, the red, white, blue, and black faces on the stage, dragging long pheasant feathers, were rushing back and forth. Knowing that they were acting out some kind of occupational dispute, I closed my eyes and tried to imagine the crude lifestyle of the ancient past.

After a while, Wu Song was brought out on stage, and the audience burst into enthusiastic cheers. The hero who had fought the tiger at Jingyang Ridge still had such power! But as I watched, I realized that the most cheers were not for the tiger-fighting scene, but for Wu Song's accusation of Pan Jinlian's flirtation with him and later for the killing of Pan Jinlian. This seemed to prove that Pan Jinlian was more hateful than the man-eating tiger, and that Wu Song was a hero especially because he could resolutely kill a charming adulteress. Is the psychology of the audience really so incomprehensible?

In all fairness, the enchanting young woman Pan Jinlian, being married to an ugly and foolish husband, flirting with Wu Song, and having an affair with Ximen Qing were not big deals. As for the later poisoning of Wu Dalang, it was only the social environment that forced her to do so. However, she unfortunately met Wu Song, who was pretentious for the sake of empty fame. First, he confessed the hidden affair to Wu Dalang, and then he cut off Pan Jinlian's head with one stroke. Finally, because of the Water Margin's painstaking efforts to portray national heroes, she became Wu Song's foil and became the archetype of a thousand-year-old adulteress. What else is there to say about these past events of feudal society?

However, in recent years, feudal ideas have been stirred up again like old wells. In today's society, from rural villages to major cities, an unknown number of women die from this every day. At the same time, tragedies of rape and murder and wife-killing are constantly emerging. And in Xiamen, there was even a father who reported his daughter's adultery, leading to his daughter's suicide! These heroes and good men can all be placed in Wu Song's ancestral hall. But if the incense of this ancestral hall is prosperous, women will have no survivors, which is very clear.

Art, with its underlying ideology, influences society, and its power is certainly greater than that of laws. The play "Wu Song" particularly emphasizes the depiction of Pan Jinlian's seductive licentiousness and Wu Song's upright extraordinariness. The emotions of the audience have been captured by it. In addition to following the right and wrong of the plot, what else can they think? I remember two years ago when I watched "Roar, China!" the cheers from the audience were far greater than those in the current "Wu Song" scene. At that time, when many male and female workers fought to the death against the imperialists, the audience was simply a chorus of hoarse cries. That kind of intense and great righteous indignation should be higher than Wu Song's killing of his sister-in-law.

However, old plays like "Wu Song" which contain feudal consciousness, are performed anytime, anywhere, while new plays like "Roar, China!" which can arouse national struggle, are as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns, one in a hundred. Isn't that strange? The most touching stage art closes off the side of liberation, and only old plays with feudal consciousness are dancing around there. In today's world of the dead acting strange, how can the audience not be even more drunk and confused when they are immersed in this aged Shaoxing wine day and night?

The Dead End of Japanese Intellectual Women 228

— Wu

The Osaka Asahi Shimbun on the 19th of this month reported: The standards Japanese employers use to select maids mostly favor those who are graduates of higher elementary schools, healthy, of amiable disposition, and have reliable guarantors. In addition, those who have worked as female entertainers or female workers, those who have not graduated from higher elementary school, those who are frail, those with family burdens, etc., are all disliked by employers. In particular, those who have graduated from middle school are most rejected by employers. The reason is that after graduating from middle school, they inevitably become ambitious and arrogant, and it is not easy for employers to control them.

From this piece of news, we can see the difficulties of Japanese women's lives. The duration of compulsory education in Japan is six years, plus four years of middle school, a woman who graduates from middle school has studied for ten years. However, middle school graduates can only be servants! Being a servant is certainly not what they want, but there is no other way to go, so they can only be servants. But employers are so harsh. This is truly the dead end of Japanese intellectual women!

Diary of a Concubine 229

— Guan Lu

June 12th

Spring, that lovely spring is already over. In that happy spring, some people were happy, some were in pain; some were in paradise, some were in prison. Some were free, some were slaves. I was in prison, acting as a slave, and spent that spring that others were happy in. No, all women are just like me. And there are those women who are even worse off than me who can't find food to eat!

The child cries every day, opening her mouth to look for milk to eat. She wants to live, to grow. She is not yet aware that she will grow into an unfortunate woman!

June 13th

These days I myself have no milk, and it's hard to hire a nanny who isn't fussy, and the child is sick. I also heard that Chief × wants us to leave the hospital in the next few days and move into the newly rented house: fortunately, the doctor told him. I and the child are not well, and there is a risk to our lives if we leave the hospital now, so Chief × didn't send anyone to urge us to leave.

In this society, women belong to men, and children belong to their parents. Women abandoned by men have nowhere to go, and children who are not cared for by their parents cannot grow up!

I remember hearing someone tell a story, saying that in some societies, women can live in society without relying on men and do things for society; they are also free to fall in love at any time. Children without parents also have state organs to support them and raise them to adulthood. But I heard it as a story, and some people say it's a fact, but I think no matter how empty the theory is, it's reasonable, and everyone should do it this way. According to what I've seen before, those charity halls and orphanages are useless. How many women who can't survive and children who wander and die number in the tens of millions every year?

June 17th

I've been dreaming these past few nights: dreaming that I'm very free, I run to an agency, and I do all the things I usually do for the people at that agency to see. They welcome me very much, saying that they want to send my child to a very good foster home, and they want me to work for them there. They pay me a salary every month; I can also visit my child during my breaks and buy her toys and candy with the money I earn. When I'm having such a dream, I'm always disturbed by a strange sound, which turns out to be the child crying beside me.

Now I'm sick, so sick that I can hardly move; but if that paradise I dreamed of can really be created, I'll get up even if I'm sick to participate in the creation, even if I die for work, it's good to make later women happy!

June 19th

Yesterday, because my temperature was too high, I said everything I was thinking about in a muddled way. The doctor therefore said that my nerves were a little abnormal. I don't think I've gone crazy, but I'm thinking too far ahead. What I think is right, people say is crazy. No, it's just that men think it's crazy. Many women haven't said that my ideas are crazy!

Today's diary is not finished, and the doctor sent someone to take away my pen. He insisted that my nerves had undergone abnormal changes and wanted me to rest without thinking at all!

Okay! You took my pen away, and that's your victory. Anyway, it's your world, and it's not fun to live in other people's worlds. Of course, I can't write a diary anymore. Now there's nothing else but for me to rest and recuperate well. When I get better, I'll settle accounts with you! After I settle accounts, I'll never be a patient or a concubine again! (The End)

Denunciation 230

— Lin Yun

The women's umbrella has only just barely managed to peek its head out from under the heavy oppression of thousands of years. This tiny, newly growing bud, still swaying uncertainly, needs doubled cultivation and maintenance. Absolutely no one should be allowed, under the guise of the women's movement, to actually destroy the growth of the women's movement and increase obstacles to women's future.

Opening our eyes, we see this women's magazine in the east and that women's publication in the west. It seems the women's movement is really flourishing, and the number of women's publications is increasing day by day. But slow down and don't get too excited. Everyone needs to examine them first.

The cover is printed with a large photograph of a woman with a seductive and charming face. Inside, it teaches women how to apply rouge, manicure their nails, and how to be charming. It also tells women which foreign brands of expensive perfume to buy. The rest consists of semi-nude pictures of women, photos of foreign movie stars, and a few erotic novels written in a "neither Chinese nor Western" style, specially prepared for men to enjoy. There are also essays telling Chinese women to catch up with the trends of modern European and American ladies. This is what is called a publication that makes women into "modern toys." There are also weekly women's periodicals, women's weekly supplements in newspapers, and miscellaneous writings about women...etc. Generally, they are nothing more than: how to cook and eat certain dishes, how to be obedient and please one's husband, so-called "husband-taming techniques," "new women's precepts," etc., teaching women to be ancient women at home, but when their husbands take them out, they must be modern women in their dress and attitude, so that their husbands' faces will shine. Otherwise, it will hurt their husbands' faces. It is a pity that it has not yet said that women should best become "Bailing machines," becoming whatever they are told to become, then the husband will really like it! Some indulge in mocking and scolding women, saying that women are trouble, that women are weak and do not strive for self-improvement, that women are born cheap, superstitious, and that women are really as cheap as dog bones, as they describe. Fortunately, women never pay attention to outside affairs, so even if they are scolded harshly, no one comes to refute them. Some point out that the ultimate path of the women's movement and women's careers is "marriage," and still attach the lock of "virtue"... A dazzling array of things, all in the name of women, but in reality, they are of no benefit to women. At the same time, for those women whose wills are not yet firm and who are struggling in hardship, they are nothing more than a kind of anesthesia and deceptive tricks of the ghosts.

We see in the daily newspapers that countless women are being abused by men, exploited by society, and wandering, suffering, and dying! Women have become extremely fragile due to thousands of years of unequal treatment, and can only be slaughtered and trampled on. Now that a little bud seems to have been exposed, how can we sit idly by and watch people release poisoned arrows without regard?

Compatriots, quickly rise up and denounce those publications that act in the name of women but actually harm the interests of women!
