Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Life

The Year-Round Hired Hand 231

— Yu Lin

In my hometown, there are two kinds of farmers: one is called "Zero-Work," meaning farmers who do not usually work for others, but are only hired to do things during the busy farming season; the other is called "Year-Round Hired Hand," meaning farmers who live in the landlord's house all year round, working for the landlord from morning till night. However, those who do "Zero-Work" mostly have a little land of their own. They take time out from their busy work to help others. The "Year-Round Hired Hands" are different. They have no land of their own, no property. All they have is a strong body and amazing strength. They work for others all month and all year. Therefore, strictly speaking, only the "Year-Round Hired Hands" can be called 100% tenant farmers. "Zero-Work" cannot be counted.

Originally, those who live in other people's houses and work for others all year round also include the "Second-in-Command" and the "Cowherd." But the "Second-in-Command" is helping the senior "Year-Round Hired Hand," not the main character, only a supporting role. The "Cowherd" is only a thirteen or fourteen-year-old child whose main job is to graze cattle, feed pigs, and do other odd jobs. They can be said to be the "junior class." Moreover, the "Second-in-Command" and the "Cowherd" work for others all month and all year round, so of course they can also be called "Year-Round Hired Hands." Therefore, the "Year-Round Hired Hands" are actually representatives of the tenant farmers. As long as we know the living conditions of the "Year-Round Hired Hands," we can imagine everything about the general tenant farmers, such as the "Second-in-Command" and the "Cowherd."

The work of the "Year-Round Hired Hands" is set in the last lunar month of the previous year. So every "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" (because their social status is very low, so people generally add the title "Erwa" after the words "Year-Round Hired Hand" to call them "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" to show their difference from "Old Master," "Great Sir," etc.) has to go to the rural market towns in the last lunar month to "be active," buying the landlords a couple of liang of shaojiu, relying on their strength, and relying on their simple and honest "nature" to obtain the "job" (meaning work) for the coming year. If the job for the coming year is secured, then their life for the year can be considered to have a "guarantee" so that there will be no danger of starvation. If, unfortunately, they have not secured a job for the coming year by the thirtieth day of the last lunar month, then they will face the terrible danger of unemployment, not knowing how to spend the year to come. Therefore, we can say that the fate of the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" is decided in the last lunar month of each year.

Now, the annual wages of the "Year-Round Hired Hands" in my hometown are roughly more than two hundred thousand copper coins. If this were in Shanghai, more than one hundred thousand copper coins could be equivalent to about one hundred silver dollars. The "Year-Round Hired Hands" live in the landlord's house all year round and eat the landlord's food. If they have an income of about one hundred yuan a year and do not have to bear the cost of rent and food, then they can be considered to be able to make a living. However, the price of silver dollars in our hometown is so high that people sitting comfortably in Shanghai simply cannot imagine it. One silver dollar there can be exchanged for more than twenty thousand copper coins. So the "Year-Round Hired Hands" who have wages of more than two hundred thousand copper coins each year actually only have an income of about ten yuan each year. Even if they do not bear the cost of rent and food and do not have family burdens, ten yuan a year is not enough.

"Work at sunrise, rest at sunset, dig a well and drink, till the field and eat." It is said that this is where the happiness of ancient farmers lies. However, the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" in my hometown now does not have any happiness. At ordinary times, they get up to work when the sky is bright. Except for eating, they are working in the fields all day long. When it comes to the season for sowing beans, they have to get up when the rooster crows, and after a quick breakfast, they have to go out to cultivate. At this time, the sun has not yet risen! During the autumn harvest, they are of course even busier and more bitter. Although it is autumn at this time, the sun is still as fierce as fire, and the weather is sometimes even hotter than summer. The work of the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" in this hot weather is to carry water rice, that is, after many farmers in the paddy field beat the rice into a large wooden bucket, they use a basket to load it up, one load at a time. The "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" carries it back to the landlord's house. This kind of water rice cannot be said to be very heavy, but it cannot be said to be very light either, probably about two hundred jin per load. The strength of the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" is of course much greater than yours and mine, so they can carry about two hundred jin of water rice all day long, without caring. In order to invigorate their bodies and liven up their hearts, the landlords specially prepare the best shaojiu and some side dishes such as pig ears and pig tongues for them at this time. Roughly, after they have carried two or three loads of water rice back, they can drink three cups of shaojiu. If we were to talk about happiness, it would probably be because they have shaojiu and pig ears to eat at this time, because these things are not easy for them to get at ordinary times.

However, we should not underestimate the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" too much. Like you, he has blood, flesh, and feelings. And, whether you believe it or not, they also talk about love! It is very interesting to say that in our hometown, the general landlords, in addition to wanting more land and more longevity, also want more children and grandchildren. As soon as they have a son, they immediately want to have a grandson. As soon as their son is twelve or thirteen years old, they want to find a way to marry him a big girl of seventeen or eighteen or even twenty-odd years old, on the one hand to have a grandson sooner, and on the other hand to have one more person at home to use! This is indeed a win-win situation. The so-called "early marriage system" is formed in this way. This early marriage system is quite beneficial to the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" because the big girl of seventeen or eighteen years old who becomes the wife of a twelve or thirteen-year-old child is certainly not satisfied. If she is not satisfied, she will seek another way out. As a result of seeking another way out, the strong and powerful "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" becomes the ideal lover. So the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" who is not supposed to talk about love talks about his love. At the same time, the daughters of the landlords are locked up at home from childhood to adulthood and are not allowed to approach men. But precisely because they cannot approach men, problems easily occur as long as there is an opportunity to approach men. The "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" often enters and exits the landlord's door and is more likely to approach the landlord's daughters. As soon as they approach, love problems easily occur. It is said that six or seven out of ten of the landlord's daughters are in love with the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa"! However, our hometown is very feudal. If the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" has a love affair with a young lady from a certain family, once discovered, the people of that family will rise up to put the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" to death, or at least break his spine to make him a cripple forever! As for having a love affair with their daughter-in-law, that cannot be generalized, because the daughter-in-law comes from another family. Even if she has a love affair with the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa," it is only ruining the reputation of another family and has nothing to do with oneself. Moreover, the utilitarianism of the landlords in our hometown is still very thorough. As they see it, the child born from the love affair between the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" and the daughter-in-law from another family is still the son of their son, still their grandson, and will never be taken away by the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa." Therefore, some landlords, when their sons are still incapable of doing anything, in order to have grandsons sooner, always pretend to be deaf and dumb about the love affair between the "Year-Round Hired Hand Erwa" and the daughter-in-law!

Overseas Correspondence Network

Elephant Hunting in Africa 232

— Du Bo

Tanta Communication from Egypt

The elephant is now the largest and most valuable animal on land. In China, except for one place in Yunnan that produces elephants, it is really not easy to see them elsewhere. But in Africa and India, elephants are as numerous as pigs. You can see them everywhere, whether in the countryside, in the fields, or on the streets.

African elephants are slightly different in shape from Indian elephants, so the methods of catching elephants are also different. African elephants have very large ears and long tusks, but they are very fierce. The captors often lose their lives if they are not careful and get flipped up by their noses. Indian elephants have small ears, only as big as a palm fan, and they are very docile. It does not take much effort to catch them. Moreover, almost all of these elephants are captured alive and can be kept as domestic animals.

There are roughly two methods of catching elephants in India. The first method is only applicable to the elephant mating season. They bring trained female elephants to the place where wild elephants are produced, and tie the four feet of the female elephant firmly with a very thick palm rope. The length of the rope is only enough for it to walk in a fixed area. In addition, many pitfalls are dug around the female elephant, and the pits are covered with leaves and palm ropes with slipknots. After arranging such a confusing array, the elephant hunters quickly hide in the forest to avoid the sight of the wild elephants.

After a while, wild elephants come walking from afar in groups of three or five or alone, thinking that the female elephant standing here is its mate. When they see that it is a female elephant, they simply rush to its side as eagerly as a horny man sees a slut, circling around it, making all kinds of frivolous and ugly gestures, and hooking up with it. In this moment of ecstatic forgetfulness, the elephant hunters fire a gun into the sky from the forest. With a "bang," the wild elephants are frightened and jump up in a panic. If they are not careful, their feet will step into

Amateur Musings

On Perseverance 233

— Li Aiting

Napoleon said: Victory often belongs to those with the most perseverance. Goldsmith said: Our greatest glory is not in maintaining perpetual failure, but in being able to rise again after each failure. Dr. Edison said: Perseverance is nineteen failures, and only success on the twentieth try. This is a fact that could not be more correct. If a person is born without the spirit of perseverance, wanting to fight against the environment, wanting to overcome all kinds of difficulties and achieve success, that would be no different from trying to climb a tree to catch fish. His lack of achievement is undeniable to anyone.

It is also a fact that a person often wants to make his career a success, but it is as if a demon is creating mischief in it. Not only is there no hope of success, but it leads to a complete defeat. Therefore, the person engaged in it inevitably becomes discouraged and falls into despair. In fact, after this effort and failure, the original substance of success has already been conceived. That is to say, if you can sacrifice a little bit and try harder, then success will immediately stand before you, and there will be no more room for hiding. Therefore, generally speaking, failure is really due to the lack of a spirit of perseverance. But what exactly is perseverance? We might as well give a definition. That is to say, the so-called perseverance is not a blind effort without a direction, but a kind of power that is formed by the combination of three things: purpose, ambition, and enthusiasm. Because when a person has a purpose, he can concentrate his power to devote himself to a certain career; when he has ambition, a kind of maintaining power can be generated for his plan; when he has enthusiasm, he can concentrate his energy to defeat all kinds of natural or man-made obstacles. These three conditions are all related to each other and absolutely cannot be separated arbitrarily. However, people in society who are generally engaged in careers, especially the impetuous young people who are new to society, often ignore this point, so that when they encounter difficulties, they lose the spirit of advancement, or even give up halfway, and finally achieve nothing, which is really a pity. At the same time, facts tell us that the use of perseverance is not only needed in a certain period of life or for a certain kind of thing, but there is a need for this spirit in any aspect. Because a person's life is just like a battlefield, inner impulses, the advantages and disadvantages of circumstances, etc., will often stimulate all kinds of fierce struggles in terms of will. At this time, if he can use perseverance to stimulate his brain and make him distinguish between right and wrong, good and evil, then he will not fall into the depths of depravity.

In the history books of ancient and modern times, I do not know how many successful great men their success never depended on chance, shortcuts, or good luck, but mostly on the spirit of perseverance. Here, we can cite two examples to prove the falsity of this statement. Peng Yang, who wrote Pilgrim's Progress, should be known to everyone! He wrote this book using the sealing paper on milk bottles. Another example is Dalais, who has become the giant in the shipping industry known to everyone today. At first, he only started with a small steamboat. I remember that Milton once said very thoroughly that the environment encountered by celebrities is mostly adverse, and that his ability to open up a path to success often requires many resistance and obstacles, so it is a great feat for a person to strive for success from the materials he has obtained. Not only were the predecessors like this, but also the people who are respected or disdained by people in various countries today will never be without the words "perseverance" in their success.

In short, perseverance is the ladder to success. If you lack this kind of perseverance, then success will never be achieved, and instead you will always be trapped in an atmosphere of real failure. Here, we can further realize that the famous teachings that failure is the mother of success and that where there is a will, there is a way are not just boring slogans, but contain considerable value.

Page 23

into the slipknot, and the more fiercely they jump, the tighter the rope on their feet becomes. In the end, they stand motionless, dejectedly waiting for the elephant hunters to come and deal with them.

The elephant hunters do not meet the wild elephants within three days after they are caught, and they do not give them food. After about a week, the elephant hunters bring food and stand at a distance, throwing it towards them, but this time they are no longer afraid of them seeing it. After three months, the wild elephants gradually become docile, so the ropes on their feet are untied and they are taken home to be kept as domestic animals.

The second method of catching elephants can be used anytime and anywhere. Although the cost is higher than the first method, the effect is much greater than the former. When using this method to catch elephants, it is necessary to look for traces of elephants everywhere in advance. If a group of wild elephants gather together, they quickly tie a long rope around the neck of the domestic elephant they are raising and drive it into the wild elephant herd to move around. The elephant hunters hide far away. After the domestic elephant has become familiar with the wild elephant herd, they slowly pull one end of the long rope towards themselves. The domestic elephant naturally walks in the direction of the rope. At the same time, the group of wild elephants also follows.

The road where this group of elephants is walking is sprinkled with fruits and other food everywhere. So the group of wild elephants unknowingly only cares about eating the food on the ground and walks leisurely. At this time, the elephant hunters lead the trained domestic elephant into a field surrounded by wooden fences. The wild elephants also follow it in a daze. Then, the elephant hunters use a very quick method to close the wooden fence door, so that the wild elephants that have entered can no longer retreat. Then, also according to the above method, the group of wild elephants is starved for a week before food is thrown to them from afar. After three or four months, this group of wild elephants becomes domestic elephants.

But in Africa, it is very difficult to catch elephants alive, because African elephants are very fierce, and it is indeed not easy to tame them, so African elephant hunters often shoot and kill them when they see them, and then come to take their teeth.

However, although there are many elephants in Africa, it is not easy to breed them. If they are shot and killed every day, there may be a day when they become extinct. Even the African wax people who live by hunting elephants have now thought of this, so everyone has agreed on a rule, the general idea of which is: "Each person cannot hunt more than three elephants a year. Female elephants must not be shot."

The method of shooting elephants with guns used by Africans seems to be easier than catching elephants in India, and it does not require much cost. However, because the elephants are different in nature, capturing dead elephants in Africa is more difficult than capturing live elephants in India. African elephant hunters gather a large group of people in advance, all carrying hunting guns, and wait in the dense forest. They first ask a few experienced hunters to survey the tracks of elephants in various forests. When he finds the elephant in what place, he immediately runs back to inform them. This kind of hunter is very respected by the general elephant hunters in Africa, and he gets particularly more private benefits after the elephant is caught.

The large group of elephant hunters receives the notification and immediately sets off with the hunter who reported the news, armed with guns and ammunition. When they are about to approach the place where the elephant is located, everyone does not dare to make a sound and squats down together. Because the elephant's sense of smell and hearing are very keen, as long as it hears a slightly different sound, it will immediately run away alertly. By the time the elephant hunters come to chase it, it will have long disappeared. So a team of elephant hunters has a leader who directs everything in the middle. The position of the elephant hunters and the way they shoot must be directed by the leader. When shooting begins, everyone stands together and aims at the common target from a distance. At the command of the leader, everyone fires their guns at the same time. After the elephant is hit by a large number of bullets, it will not be able to support itself and will fall down. If individual shooting in a skirmish line style is used, it is very dangerous. Because the physique of an elephant can never be subdued by the power of one or two bullets. If it is hit by a shot and does not die, it will immediately rush to the place where the shooting is taking place. If someone is seen by it at this time, his life will be over. No matter where you escape to, it will never fall down until it chases you. Elephant hunting requires a large group of people to go together to avoid this danger. Because there are many people, shooting together, the firepower is fierce. Even if people are seen by it, it has no way to chase them because there are too many people.

In Africa, in addition to the local natives, there are also many white people who engage in this kind of adventurous life from time to time. The value of ivory is not very high in Africa, but once it is transported to the United States and Europe, the difference is several times as much. Therefore, for the sake of high profits, white people do not hesitate to send their lives to Africa to gamble with elephants. White people come here to hunt elephants, mostly in teams of three or five. When they get close to the elephant-producing area, they hire local natives to help them catch them, agreeing on a reward of how much money per day. However, if the hired natives lose their lives due to elephant hunting, the white people are not responsible.

The main purpose of white people coming here is ivory. They often spend several months or even a whole year without starting to hunt elephants, but only specialize in looking for places where dead elephants are found. If that kind of place is found, the ivory they get is more than the ivory teeth shot down in a year. After all, white people are smart. This situation can probably be seen often in foreign animal films that are screened in China.

The Scenery of Great Shanghai

Impressions of the London Exhibition 234

— Tuo

The pedestrians on the road seemed even more active. He, I, and Ping, Xiu, jumped onto a Route 1 tram, which was even more crowded. We got off and stepped onto the stone steps of the Bank of China, dropping a few silver dollars into a hole in exchange for three admission tickets.

"Ah, this is a moment of pride for the great nation of our ancient civilization! Even the yellow-haired, green-eyed devils have to come and see the civilization of our ancient Eastern country, you fake connoisseurs!"

"Heh heh heh!"

This was a conversation between a fellow with a walrus mustache and a young man in a sharp suit. The young man chuckled and strode in, tap-tap-tap.

First Room – Exhibiting the "Throne" once sat upon by our ancestors, the rulers.

"Truly extraordinary. Ping, what do you think? You have a good eye. Look, a purple dais inlaid with cloisonné cloud-pattern throne, wow, a gilded wooden footrest. The gold isn't yellow enough, is it? What do you say?"

Ping and Xiu silently squeezed through the crowd. The walrus mustache grumbled again: "I don't believe that sitting on the Emperor's throne will really make you dizzy? Damn it, if there weren't chains holding it down, I would definitely sit on it, damn it."

"Ha ha, are you still dreaming of being an emperor?" said the young man in the suit. But the walrus mustache still harbored a wistful feeling of being so close yet so far away.

"Screen – That is a sandalwood screen inlaid with cloisonné immortal mountains and pavilions. Oh, oh." The ancient, thread-bound catalog rustled in dry, claw-like fingers.

"Liu Yong, Weng Fanggang, these few famous Qing Dynasty favorites!" Another middle-aged man with gold-rimmed glasses perched on his nose pushed them up and bent down, touching his nose to the edge of the redwood painting table. "Yes, it can't escape Weng Fanggang's brush." Dry, claw-like fingers stroked the edge of the table again, shell, shell, shell – then tapped on the surface.

Small writing brushes, white jade brush holders, white jade inkstones, white jade seals, white jade brush rests, white jade melon-shaped water containers, everything was made of white jade.

Where did we wander into? Oh, right, the calligraphy and painting room of the Tang, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties.

"Open the catalog, Ping. This is the calligraphy and painting room. Check the calligraphy and painting catalog, what number? Okay, this one." I narrowed my eyes, staring and staring, then walked further away to look again. Good, very good indeed.

"Maple trees stand aloof - the mountain is even clearer - a long beach with shallow rapids - intersecting horizontally. Two old men - sit peacefully with nothing on their minds, quietly watching the reeds - grow on the other shore. The poetic imagery is also unrestrained and fresh, good poem!" Ping praised.

"Damn it, what the emperor did was too much. Not to mention how many innocent lives were lost at his hands, how much people's blood and sweat he sucked into his belly. Look, just one good, complete piece of art, and as soon as it gets into his hands, he stamps that 'Seal of Imperial Inspection by Qianlong' on it, like a big block of tofu, spoiling the color so much! Look, this red block on top of the mountain peak is so discordant!" Xiu sighed greatly, and everyone's face lengthened.

A great piece of art, I couldn't stand there and feast on its beauty alone, the tide of people rushed me past.

"This painting by the Manchus is not bad! – Hazy mists at sunset, I'll copy it down, this inscription is not bad either; Autumn grass and yellow flowers – covering old paths, hidden forest – where – does smoke rise, a mountain monk alone grows old in the mountains, only seeing – cold pines – see youth! The wonder lies in the last two lines! Chinese painting is like this, the writing must rely on the beauty of the words to complement its beauty!"

We sat down and started chatting:

"Su Hanchen's 'Autumn Garden Children at Play,' Liu Songnian's 'Five Scholars,' I don't know what's so good about them. What's so good about Tang Bohu's apricot blossoms? Heaven knows!"

"On the other hand, several paintings depicting scenes in a rainstorm are all good, tense and meticulous. I like those the most: Li Di's 'Returning Cattle in Wind and Rain,' Gao Kegong's 'Rainy Mountain,' and Lin Tinggui's 'Misty Rain,' Dai Jin's 'Returning Boat in Wind and Rain.' Maybe it's my prejudice, but it seems that this description of the agitated state in a rainstorm is enough to reflect today's era. If those elegant and leisurely things are displayed in this turbulent world again, they seem too far removed from the times."

"That's part of the reason. In fact, there are also some small pieces of leisure and sadness that are more exquisite than the large pieces. Don't you remember? Last year we saw that withered tree painted by Ni Zan at the Ningbo hometown association. It was so light and vigorous. But this time, Ni Zan's things are simply not good."

"Small pieces? Xu Wei's pomegranates are still quite lovely. His inscription is good: Deep in the mountains, ripe stones crack open, smiling towards the sun, few people pick them, relying on bright pearls to walk. Writing about ripe pomegranates, it can be said to be very lifelike."

"What do you think of Emperor Uncle's ink Zhong Kui?"

"Haha, that wisp of beard is really seemingly stable and seemingly present, seemingly existing and seemingly not, but the brushwork seems still vigorous."

The wave-like crowd was rolling in front of us, and we also "went up another floor." Stepping on the marble steps, thinking about the colorful antiques, I unconsciously forgot my original face before entering the ivory tower.

The top floor was just as crowded with people. I caught a glimpse of Mr. So-and-so, one of the giants of the Cunwen Association. He was lifting his long beard, holding his old reading glasses in his palm, rubbing his inflexible eyes, "Flat, flat, oblique, oblique, oblique, flat, flat, oblique, oblique, flat, flat, oblique…"

Emperor Uncle's masterpieces are always the easiest to attract attention. That girl hanging on the arm of a young gentleman like a clerk, while showing her iron fingers to the young gentleman, was putting her little finger in her little mouth, so charming. —

——Garments and hats in dreams, what auspiciousness? The Ming Dynasty has a long heritage. Who compares him to the previous incarnation of Han Yu, writing articles for him with the writing brush.

This is imperial calligraphy. Awkward handwriting, but it is imperial calligraphy, so it also represents Chinese art. Again, the Emperor's imperial calligraphy:

——A branch of residual snow shines on the mountain city, the spring spirit is originally not renewed later, ashamed to use red face to flatter children, plum brother knows my cold years affection.

Emperor Uncle is also a human being, definitely not cold-blooded. Right! Then why do you show such a cold and frosty face to the people?

There were too few "words." Squeezing into a corner, I saw two album pages of calligraphy by Huang Tingjian displayed in a glass case that satisfied me. The writing was transcendent and refined, and the brushwork was concise and meticulous, even more proud than the nearby Su Shi's.

Walking back, I saw two portraits. A certain emperor of the Yuan Dynasty and two empresses of the Yuan Dynasty. Strange, the empress's eyebrows were painted as thin and long as the girls who visited the art exhibition in the 24th year of the Republic of China, but the empress who grew up in the desert of flying sand and cracked skin was not very fashionable after all. A straight black line is really not as beautiful as a curve.

Following the crowd, we poured into another room with displays.

Many heads were bowed over the glass cases, squatting down to see what was below. Pointing and gesturing, laughing.

"Old brother, if you and I had such a thing, we wouldn't have to be worried all day long!"

That "thing" was wearing a melon-skin cap, looking like a small merchant. The person being called "old brother" couldn't stop laughing, and pressed his face even closer to the glass cabinet.

Looking over, there were too many names to remember clearly! What a "li," a "ding," a "lan," a "zuan," a "dou," a "fu," a "hu," a "you," and then what corners, jue, ..., gu, zhi, zun, pan, jian, yi, zhong, bo, zheng, nao, ling, duo, ge, mao, sword – just the categories of bronze ware alone were so many, and each name had so many strange and varied forms. Okay, let's take a quick look and broaden our horizons.

"Haha, Father Xin Li, Island-patterned Fang Li, are they all Shang Dynasty artifacts? Such a distant age!"

"What kind of ding is this? Oh, oh, let me see, yes, Taotie Ding, look how big it is!"

This old gentleman actually went to touch it with his withered hand, touching the glass.

"Country bumpkin! Old fool!" This voice came from who knows where, softly.

"Hahaha." It rang out. The old gentleman widened his eyes and looked around.

The inscriptions on the dark brown bronze ware, although not clear, were very clear on the white paper rubbings. The calligraphy was extremely beautiful. This is probably what is called the inscription on the mirror ding.

"It's a pity that Mr. Bao Lu didn't come with us today, otherwise he could definitely point out a lot to us, right?" Ping said, seemingly very regrettable!

"Yes, we are all laymen, but these words can probably only be recognized by Bao Lu!" Xiu said.

"Not necessarily, maybe he still can't fully recognize them. Many archaeologists can't recognize them!"

"Then, he is much more knowledgeable than us!" I said.

Talking like this, we had already walked past several counters displaying porcelain and jade. These were all things that the rulers had searched for from their slaves and obedient people by virtue of their authority. Thinking of the emperors who, at that time, gathered the whole world to themselves, their luxurious and dissolute lives, and their wanton attitude of taking and seizing, I couldn't help but feel sad. However, the throne finally fell, and the treasures in the Forbidden City were finally displayed in front of the descendants of those who had been suppressed under authority. Isn't this the greatness of the era?

Amateur Studies

On the Attitude of Reading 235

— Xue

Mr. Yang Weiyu recently published an article in the special issue of "Reading Problems" in the 25th volume, number 3, of the "Education Magazine," advocating "reading for the sake of reading." The general idea of the original text is: "…Nowadays, most people read with a purpose. If we analyze it, some read for the sake of awakening the world and helping the people, some for the sake of fame and wealth, some for the sake of application, some for the sake of self-cultivation, some for the sake of appreciation, and some for the sake of studies. On the surface, it seems that there are sufficient reasons, but in a nutshell, their reading is all 'for something.' I believe that reading 'for something' is not true reading. It is using reading as a tool, as a means to achieve a certain purpose. It is like students studying for a graduation certificate, and writers writing books for copyright. Of course, there are exceptions, but at least some people put down the tools after the purpose is achieved. Such reading, at most, increases some information in terms of knowledge, and is far from the true meaning of reading. Those who lead learning learn for the sake of learning, and true readers should also read for the sake of reading, that is, reading 'for nothing.'…" Mr. Yang's attitude in this article is that of a "reading supremist." He advocates "true readers reading for the sake of reading," and advocates "reading for nothing." He opposes reading with a purpose, and denies reading "for application," "for self-cultivation," and "for appreciation."

Previously, we knew that Mr. Yang was a vocational educator. Vocational educators have always been proponents of utilitarian education. They have criticized the separation of education and life, and have vigorously advocated education for livelihood, education that combines manual and mental labor, and education in practical skills such as industry, agriculture, and commerce. But judging from this article, Mr. Yang's thinking seems to be very different from before.

In ancient China, apart from those who were obsessed with fame and fortune, there were indeed a few scholars who read for the sake of reading. They regarded reading as the best way to spend leisure time, and regarded the qin, chess, calligraphy, and painting as entertainment. As the saying goes, "There are golden houses in books, and there are beauties like jade in books." They absolutely isolated themselves from the world, absolutely isolated themselves from the times, living comfortably and leisurely, enjoying a life of luxury, and regarding the profit-making activities of all farmers, workers, and merchants as lowly. Most of the ancient readers who "read for the sake of reading" were like this. Because the scholar-official class who read for the sake of reading lived in an environment of leisure, abundance, and food, they had the blessings of their ancestors to enjoy, and had a special situation where they did not have to fight with real life. They did not need a skill to receive a good life, so their reading was completely individualistic, and never had the slightest connection with society and the masses. Perhaps they made some discoveries in the ivory tower, but these discoveries did not contribute to history or mankind!

Today, I dare say that it is definitely not that era. Today's youth, especially the youth of that class, is not. Today's youth must read to improve their living skills, and must read to strengthen the development of their body and mind. Reading and painting must be integrated with real life to be interesting and effective. Those who read for the sake of reading only see mirages in the sky, and can only let the blessed young masters appreciate and praise them.

Most of the young people who have already entered society are mostly regretting that the books they read in school cannot be applied to practical use and are too far away from the world of life. This is because they did not read for the sake of life at that time.

When a person studies at school, he should enrich his knowledge in line with his life goals. Even those who serve in society still have to work hard to study for the sake of improving their business, and will never "put down the tools after the purpose is achieved" as Mr. Yang said. Moreover, their reading will never only be for the sake of reading, and the interest in reading does not necessarily have to be increased by "reading for the sake of reading." Only reading for the sake of solving business difficulties may be more intense than the empty "there are golden houses in books" style of reading because of a sense of "need."

The meaning of "interest lies in the source of needs" that I mentioned above has the best evidence. To give a simple example, the teaching methods in elementary schools used to be injection-style lectures, and the children's responsiveness was very weak, even feeling only pain and not interest. Now, the heuristic method that is advocated uses a kind of motivation to make children feel a certain need and learn, and their interest is naturally much stronger. Also, educational psychologist Peterson once conducted an experiment in which he wrote a lot of words on the blackboard and told the students to copy them. Afterwards, he told them to recite them silently, and after a while, he told them to recite them silently again. This was the first experiment. Another type of experiment was to notify the students in advance that they would copy it once, and then recite it later, and then do it again according to the first method. As a result, the second experiment was much better than the first. It can be seen that the first experiment did not know the need and was copying for the sake of copying, so the results were poor. The second knew the need and was copying for the need, so the results were good.

The reading concept of "studying for a graduation diploma" is indeed wrong, and the reading concept of "reading for fame and fortune" is indeed wrong, but if you say that reading for the sake of application or self-cultivation is not right, then that is really wrong!

Celebrity Biography

The Pure Poet Shelley (3) 236

— Written by Japanese Tsurumi Yusuke, Translated by Zhou Leshan and Qi Junfu

At this time, his sisters in the girls' school dormitory secretly gave him their own pocket money, so Shelley was spared from starving to death in London.

He often went to the school to see his sisters. On the days when Shelley, who resembled the god Apollo, visited, there was a great commotion in the girls' school. As usual, he wore loose blond hair, wore a throat-revealing shirt, and his coat pockets were filled with biscuits and raisins, bulging outwards. He visited his sisters like a spring breeze.

Then he would tell the female students about his school of justice and beauty.

Among them was a beautiful girl named Harriet Westbrook. Her father was the owner of a hotel, a nouveau riche. This girl secretly loved Shelley. But Shelley, who was as innocent as a young boy, did not notice this.

His uncle was a retired naval colonel with a forthright personality. Through the mediation of this uncle, his father

Page 24

Page 25

was willing to give him two thousand pounds a year, so he could bury himself in London and read the books he loved.

The following summer, he received a passionate letter from Hai Li. In the letter, she said that everyone in the school laughed at her for being a hotel girl, so she no longer wanted to live in the dormitory. But her father wanted her to return to school no matter what. She felt that life was boring and that it would be better to commit suicide and be done with it. Finally, she said that Shelley should take her away with him. Shelley panicked and went down the mountain to visit her in London. In many ways, Shelley's thinking was different from ordinary people. He did not have the youthful sexual attraction to women, and he did not love Hai Li. However, the sixteen-year-old girl's kind love, after being revealed, made him, who was not concerned with his own interests, feel that he had to save her no matter what. Originally, it would be a great loss to society for a descendant of the nobility to marry a hotel girl, and there were countless women who admired him, but the extraordinarily pure-hearted he was determined to devote himself to this girl's ardent love.

So a nineteen-year-old youth and a sixteen-year-old girl eloped to Scotland and got married on Edinburgh Street. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

The Process of Filming the Newsreel of the Hauptmann Kidnapping Trial (Part 1) 242

— Xin Ni

At the beginning of this year, the biggest news in the United States was the trial of Hauptmann, the kidnapper who kidnapped and murdered the young son of Colonel Lindbergh, the hero who first successfully flew across the Atlantic. Hauptmann was originally from Germany and had lived in the United States for many years, working as a carpenter. Somehow, he came up with the idea of kidnapping the beloved son of Colonel Lindbergh, the hero whom the American people unanimously admired for his successful first flight across the Atlantic. Later, because the search in various places was very urgent and he could not hide, he killed the child and abandoned the body in the wilderness. After the case was solved, after many trials, he was finally sentenced to death.

The Hauptmann case was tried in a local court in Flemington, New Jersey. This was a sensational trial in the United States. During the trial, the major American news agencies telegraphed the situation in the courtroom to countries around the world every day. Our Chinese newspapers also published reports on this case every day. In this way, the American newsreel companies certainly did not want to let it go.

We can now describe and discuss two questions about the filming of the Hauptmann kidnapping case. One is whether there were any illegal aspects in the process of filming the Hauptmann case. The second question is whether the newsreel of the Hauptmann case should have been filmed. These two questions are of great value for discussion in the production of newsreels, and they are worthy of attention by those involved in the production of newsreels.

Regarding the first point, some people at the time raised the question of whether it was illegal or not, and Prosecutor General Wilentz also stated that if the photographers disobeyed orders, the court would file a contempt of court lawsuit against the film company. Some people say that the production of such newsreels was originally illegal and could not be openly filmed, and that the Hauptmann case newsreels currently being screened by various film companies were filmed illegally and secretly. In short, they used tricks, secrecy, and breach of trust to achieve considerable results.

What is the real situation? Of course, only those who personally filmed the film on the scene know. So someone took this question and asked Clifford, the person in charge of filming the Hauptmann case for Universal Newsreel, who told the situation at the time without hesitation.

He said, "There was no falsehood or deception involved." He took out a photo from the courtroom and pointed it out to the interviewer. "That is the camera that filmed the Hauptmann case newsreel. Standing next to it is cameraman Dan Oliver. That is the camera's mobile box, four feet square and two feet thick. Of course, these things cannot be hidden."

In this way, we can know that the newsreel of the Hauptmann case was not filmed illegally and secretly, but how was the sound recorded? According to the "Hollywood" reporter Virgil, the recording machine was hidden under the judge's table, but that is also inaccurate.

Clifford specially invited recording engineer George Graham to describe the content of the recording at the time, because he was the technician who recorded on the spot.

George Graham said: "That's a joke, impossible. People who say this don't know the principles of recording. If the recording machine was placed under the judge's table, all that could be recorded would be a muffled buzzing sound. The noise of the entire courtroom would be recorded in a chaotic manner. But what we recorded was a very clear speech."

According to George's statement, their recording machine was installed on the wall, where everyone could see it. Behind the recording machine, there was also a semicircular cardboard that could be rotated to directly face the place where the sound was coming from. One day, a court clerk deliberately tore off the cardboard. Later, George spent two dollars to have another court clerk reinstall it. Of course, there was no secret involved.

Clifford also said: "Before the Hauptmann case trial began, five major companies held a meeting to discuss the cooperation plan." He took out a piece of paper from the drawer and said, "This is the contract we all signed. We have three large cameras, one installed in the courtroom, one in the courtroom library, and one on the front balcony of the courthouse. These three things are visible to everyone, and the recording machine's wires are a foot thick, which is also very eye-catching, with no concealment whatsoever.

"Furthermore, it has been published in newspapers that when the first night court session was held, the lights in the court suddenly went out completely. Do you know how it happened? It turned out that the 'photo floodlights' used for filming in the court caused the power to be too strong, and the main power line was blown. Later, the floodlights were not used, and 300-watt light bulbs were used instead, so there was no second incident. Of course, everyone in the courtroom knew that someone was filming." (To be continued)

Movie Review

Review of "Clive of India" 243

— You Jing

Clive of India

Speaking of Robert Clive, the hero who conquered India.

We really need to briefly touch on the "History of the Fall of India." Ever since Diaz and Vasco da Gama and Columbus discovered America-like discoveries of India, the Portuguese fleet was the first to arrive, and then the Dutch, French, and British followed suit, establishing the East India Company and engaging in aggressive competition on this incredibly rich peninsula. Due to the determination of the subjective conditions of each country, only France became Britain's last strong enemy. They first used the Indian indigenous princes to exclude the British, and then directly used troops to seize the British bases. After repeated defeats, the British army was fortunate to have Clive come out to turn defeat into victory and subdue the French, stipulating that India must not station French troops. As a result, the British influence expanded to the whole of India. Subsequently, the King of Bengal, Suraj Ud Dowlah, rose up to wage a war of resistance against aggression, and the British again recalled Clive, who had returned to his homeland, and he used enticement to induce the king's uncle, Mir Jafar, to rebel and win the war. This is the famous Battle of Plassey in 1757 in history. From then on, Bengal became British territory, and East India became the general mechanism for political and economic aggression. The person in charge used Clive's old trick of provoking discord and inducing and threatening the indigenous princes, and by 1857 the whole of India had completely become a colony.

The film "Clive of India" is based on this historical story. In today's world, with the deepening of the economic panic, the fierce competition for sales markets, and at the same time, the rapidly changing situation and the approaching war opportunities, the colonial liberation movement is gradually surging, and the ambitious aggressors dream day and night of obtaining a few more colonial lands to divide in order to solve the international deadlock of political economy that is paralyzed, and at the same time, they also hope for the rebirth of a Clive-style hero to manage and suppress the shaking colonies, so the appearance of this "Clive of India" has become a hunger-relieving product and a stimulant for these dreams and expectations.

"Clive of India" on the one hand is a passionate recollection of the aggressors, a vague yearning, and on the other hand, it is also a demonstration against the self-reliance movement of the weak nations that are being shaken. Therefore, in "Clive of India," we can only see a shadow of the demise of India revealed from the side of the heroic feats, and we can only appreciate the breath of the weak nations from the delicate cries and slight anger of the beauties.

That "Clive of India" has become a film like this is by no means accidental. The playwright distorted the historical significance, erased the objective background, and while emphasizing Clive's personal heroism, he even exaggerated his and his virtuous wife Margaret's tender love, and this attempt was to slightly conceal the intentions we pointed out above. Because of this, the great historical material, which is as brightly colored and bloody as possible, has formed an ordinary war romance film. He spared no effort to depict the hero Clive and to show off the beautiful ladies, virtuous mothers, and good wives like Margaret. The author may think that this is the best of both worlds, but he does not know that he has lost a greater achievement.

The subtitles here seem to be too many. In the production of some historical dramas, the use of subtitles is originally a last resort, but here the playwright is overly biased towards the protagonist Clive himself and uses too many subtitles to replace some pictures. Writing about Clive's initial ambition and writing about Margaret's really rushing over after receiving a love letter from a stranger, these important personality characteristics have not been properly and fully dealt with.

Director Richard Boleslawski's technique is commendable. He wrote about the Clive couple in detail without being tiresome, and he wrote about the surroundings in a lively manner without being simple. The bird's-eye view of the besieged British soldiers and the bird's-eye view of the licentious music in the Indian palace show great power. It's just that the big scene in the House of Commons seems dull and sluggish.

In terms of acting, I have to recommend Loretta Young's expression in the scene where Margaret first meets Clive. Judging from the whole play, her acting as a naive and enthusiastic girl is better than acting as a sophisticated and rational young woman. Colman's scene when he was being judged in court was a failure. The makeup of Edmund, the brother-in-law, is too careless. The hairstyles of the sisters have aged several times, so why is he still so young and has not added any wrinkles?

New Developments in Science and Art - Performances of Color Stereoscopic Films 244

— Zhi

In recent years, the perfect success and progress of film science and art have undeniably given film audiences a deep understanding and appreciation. Recently, in the progress of film art, there has been a new discovery that has attracted great attention from the world. This is the success of color stereoscopic films.

Since the history of film in the nineteenth century, the creation of color films has gone through several periods of gradual progress. Until now, after years of experimentation, this perfect color stereoscopic film has finally been successful, and the completely natural color "Dancing Partner" has now met us.

For the past twenty-five years, countless methods have been tried for the production of color films. However, the results obtained have never been fully satisfactory. Although the colors of ordinary color positives and cartoons, from the audience's point of view, are mostly already considered to be bright and pleasing to the eye. However, strictly speaking from a technical point of view, these colors have not yet reached the pinnacle of success.

The current method of color stereoscopic film is based on the three-color method. The difference between the three-color system is that the former uses two sets of negatives to print on one film. But now, when shooting a film, three sets of negatives are used to shoot the same target at the same time. The basic colors used are one set of red, one set of yellow, and one set of blue. Because three different positions of lenses are used to capture and print into one film, the same thing is projected. Thus, a stereoscopic image is formed.

A few months ago, after RKO's producer, Merlin Cooper, considered this method of color film, he knew that color film would definitely increase the audience's emotions and the entertainment value of the film itself. After John H. Whitney, the inventor of color stereoscopic photography, successfully experimented, he collaborated with his cousin, Wendeby, to produce the film. Also, because of the importance of color composition in the film, he retained the world-famous stage designer Robert Edmond Jones to preside over it. Mr. Jones felt infinite interest in this emerging art and wanted to contribute some valuable works to society with his experience in color composition and harmony. Later, "Dancing Partner" was completed, and he has achieved great success. And he received the 1934 award from the World Academy of Sciences and Arts.

Hanna McCowan, the producer of "Little Women," is also the producer of this film. This time, Mrs. Carrie also worked hard to help him with his work. The director is Roy Liggin. The photographer is Leinan Zhihan. He is one of the most famous color film photographers.

Last autumn, the company already had a plan to shoot feature films using color stereoscopic technology. So this "Dancing Partner" is the forerunner of future color stereoscopic feature films. The heroine is Ms. Steve Dona, the Hungarian girl who starred in "Flower of the Isle." The hero is Don Alvarez, who is famous for his Spanish dance. The other supporting roles are also the best choices in Hollywood.

Tong Yuejuan Sacrifices Golden Teeth 245

Tong Yuejuan, a good girl on the red felt couch, previously played a singing girl in the sound film "Red Sheep Hero Biography" by Xinhua Film Company. With a green scarf covering her head and wearing old cloth clothes, she washed away the powder and the fragrance of silk that she usually had. Director Yang Xiaozhong believed that the charm of her expression and the truth of her performance showed that she was a very promising talent. This time, when filming "The Peach Blossom Fan," director Ouyang Yuqian also thought that it was most appropriate for Tong to play the protagonist Xie Sufang in the play. Tong was very interested in the work of the silver screen and readily agreed. However, Tong's pearly teeth were inlaid with gold, and she was deeply afraid that this dazzling thing would enter the lens and turn black, like it was about to fall out. So she resolutely removed the golden teeth, and the filming will begin in the next few days.

Recent News from Shanghai Sound Film Company 246

Shanghai Sound Film Company has been working very hard recently to film "Peach Blossom Dream." This play was written by Zheng Yimei, directed by Du Yu, and starred Yin Mingzhu. Although Yin has starred in many films, it is still the first time for her to speak in a sound film.

"Peach Blossom Dream" contains the "Song of the World of Money," written by Li Jinhui, which is extremely satirical.

Cang Yinqiu, Ying Yin, Zhou Fengwen, Dan Pinpin, etc. all play important roles in "Peach Blossom Dream."

Overthrowing women's vanity and exposing the evils of society are the sole purposes of "Peach Blossom Dream." Therefore, it was praised by the Film Censorship Committee during the initial review.

Movie Novel

Hate in the Clouds (Living on Velvet) (8) 247

— Ti Yun

Thorne's eyes were closed, but his fingers groped for Amy's hand, holding it tightly. He gasped slightly and said, "Amy... marry Walt... he is a good guy... Walt..." Amy almost cried when she heard this, but she managed to hold back and said, "I want to marry you... marry you again... as long as you want me... Thorne, my love..."

Thorne wanted to laugh, but at this moment, a sharp pain suddenly invaded his heart. Amy turned her head to the side, unable to bear to look any further. Thorne's voice was even weaker, but he still said intermittently: "Want to call me... speech... topic... death... death is stupidly painted... how to deal with it... not bad... I..." His voice gradually disappeared into the void. His eyes were still closed, but one of his hands loosened and fell down.

Amy was still kneeling beside him. She knew that everything was in the past. There was nothing in the world that she could care about anymore. But she knelt there without moving, until Walt quietly walked up to her and gently helped her up.

Thorne died in the summer. But the summer quietly passed, autumn scraped the leaves off the trees, and winter came again, covering the earth with a layer of white velvet. During these difficult years, Walt stood by her side forever, helping her and caring for her with the warmth of friendship, never leaving her.

It was another snowy afternoon, and Walt and Amy sat silently on a park bench. Amy's eyes were fixed on the cars coming and going, unconsciously fascinated by them. Walt stood aside, quietly looked at her for a while, and then said, "Amy, we should go. It could rain at any time in this kind of weather." Amy said, "I like the rain..."

Everyone was silent for a while, and Walt couldn't help but call out to her, "Amy..." Amy said, "Yes, my love?" Walt stammered, "Think about it, I think it's best to... forget him... don't think about him." Amy slowly raised her head, looked at Walt's face, and put both hands in his hands. She said, "But, Walt, I have forgotten... everything about him, I have forgotten... everything! Look, I decided to forget... and I really forgot!"

Walt patted her hand, and they looked at each other in silence, but understood each other's hearts. They stood up and slowly walked out of the garden. Walt called a streetcar. Amy tightly hugged Walt's arm. Walt would never disappoint her. He would put peace in her heart... he could give her a guarantee. That's right, she had indeed forgotten Thorne.

As she walked, she muttered to herself: "Forgetfulness, Walt, that's what an Indian chief taught me... he lives in the Black Hills of Dakota... I'm very friendly with him... before he died, he taught me that secret..."

A streetcar stopped by the road. Walt helped Amy into the car, and then jumped in himself. It was the dim yellow dusk, and the car soon disappeared into the white snow. (The End)
